        <meta property="og:url" content="https://pubs.acs.org/doi/full/10.1021/acsami.7b14946"><meta property="og:title" content="An All-Phosphate and Zero-Strain Sodium-Ion Battery Based on Na3V2(PO4)3 Cathode, NaTi2(PO4)3 Anode, and Trimethyl Phosphate Electrolyte with Intrinsic Safety and Long Lifespan"><meta property="og:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/acsami.7b14946.social.jpeg_v03"><meta property="og:description" content="Development of intrinsically safe and long lifespan sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is urgently needed for large-scale energy storage applications. However, most of the currently developed SIBs suffer from insufficient cycle life and potential unsafety. Herein, we construct an all-phosphate sodium-ion battery (AP-SIB) using a Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode, NaTi2(PO4)3 anode, and nonflammable trimethyl phosphate (TMP) electrolyte. The AP-SIB exhibits not only high safety, high rate performance, and ultralong cycle life but also zero-strain characteristics due to the inverse volume change of the phosphate cathode and anode during charge and discharge cycles, offering a safer and cycle-stable Na-ion technology for electric storage applications."><meta property="og:type" content="Article"><meta property="og:site_name" content="ACS Publications"><meta name="twitter:card" content="summary_large_image"><meta name="twitter:site" content="@ACSPublications"><meta name="twitter:image" content="https://pubs.acs.org/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/acsami.7b14946.social.jpeg_v03">

<!-- loading Javascript for using the persistence Service -->
    <script src="/wro/nwyw~thiss-ds.js" async="" nonce="90f6e9c81d48775c-SJC"></script>

    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e9c81d48775c-SJC">

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            timeout: 5000,

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
            },
            retrieveEntity: function (ms) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                if (ms == undefined || ms === '') {
                    ms = this.timeout;
                }

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res.data);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('failed to retrieve entity from local storage: ' + err);
                        });
                    // Set up the timeout
                    setTimeout(function () {
                        reject('Promise timed out ' + ms + ' ms');
                    }, ms);
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    persistService.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage due to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {
                            doi: doi,
                            entityid: entityId,
                            entityTitle: entityTitle,
                            eventGroupKey: '99f69c09-972f-40b8-91f1-2377fa51e6d2'
                        }

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    }).fail(function (status) {
                        return reject(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (i = 0; i < allSsoInstitutions.length; i++) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        if(allSsoInstitutions.length === 0 && true){
                            self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, null, null)
                                .then(function () {
                                    console.log('No Entity found');
                                }, function (err) {
                                    console.log('failed to get the none entity status' ,err);
                                });
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            }).catch(function (err) {
                                reject(err);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();

                    if ($('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').length > 0) {
                        let institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox = $('.institution-preference-userconsent-checkbox').get(0);
                        if (!$(institutionPreferenceUserConsentCheckbox).is(":checked")) {
                            return;
                        }
                    }

                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

    </script>

<script type="text/javascript" nonce="90f6e9c81d48775c-SJC">
var dfpReady = false;
$(document).ready(function() {
    // var journalTitle = 'applied_materials_interfaces';
    var taxonomyKeywords = $('.article_header-taxonomy');
    var articleKeyword = $('meta[name="keywords"]');
    var articleTitle = $('meta[name="dc.Title"]');
    var articleDescription = $('meta[name="dc.Description"]');
    var abstractKeyword = $('p.articleBody_abstractText:contains("Keywords: ")');
    var searchTerms = [];

    if (taxonomyKeywords.length > 0) {
        $(taxonomyKeywords).children(".rlist--inline").children("li").each(function() {
            searchTerms.push($(this).text());
        });
    }
    else if (articleKeyword.length > 0) { 
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleKeyword.prop('content').split(', '));
    }
    else if (abstractKeyword.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(abstractKeyword.text().split("Keywords: ")[1].split('; '));
    }
    else if (articleDescription.length > 0) {
        $(articleDescription).each(function() {
            articleDescriptionKeywords = $(this).prop('content');
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/.,/g,"");
            articleDescriptionKeywords = articleDescriptionKeywords.replace(/\s{2,}/g," ");
            searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleDescriptionKeywords.split(' '));
        });
    }

    if (articleTitle.length > 0) {
        searchTerms = searchTerms.concat(articleTitle.prop('content').split(' '));
    }

    googletag.cmd.push(function() {
        var mappingLeader = googletag.sizeMapping().
        addSize([750, 200], [728, 90]). 
        addSize([0, 0], [320, 50]).
        build();
        //leaderboard
        googletag.defineSlot('/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article', [728, 90], 'dfp-journal-article-leaderboard').defineSizeMapping(mappingLeader).setTargeting('location', 'leaderboard1').setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //recommend
        googletag.defineSlot("/8868/journal/applied_materials_interfaces/article", [1, 1], "dfp-journal-article-recommend").setTargeting("ntvPlacement", ["1100167"]).setTargeting("location", "recommend").setTargeting('Keyword', searchTerms).addService(googletag.pubads());
        //googletag.pubads().enableSingleRequest();
        googletag.pubads().collapseEmptyDivs();
        googletag.pubads().setTargeting('inst',dartInstitutionType).setTargeting('memb',dartMember);
        googletag.pubads().addEventListener("slotRenderEnded", function(event) {
            console.log(event.slot.getSlotElementId() + " isEmpty: " + event.isEmpty + " | creative id: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            if((event.isEmpty === false) && (event.slot.getSlotElementId() != "dfp-journal-article-recommend")) {
                $("#" + event.slot.getSlotElementId()).parents(".advertisement").slideDown();
                console.log("ad display: " + event.creativeId + " " + event.size[0] + "x" + event.size[1]);
            }
            // else {
            //     console.log("no ad found");
            // }
        });
        googletag.enableServices();
        dfpReady = true;
    });
});
</script>

<script nonce="90f6e9c81d48775c-SJC">
$(function() {
    var serialCode = "aamick";
    var books = ["reagents", "symposium", "advances", "medichemreviews", "styleguide"]
    if(books.includes(serialCode) === false) {
        // default click action
        $("[data-id]").on("mousedown", function(e) {
            var currentClickID = $(this).attr("data-id");

            if(currentClickID.includes("_hover") === false) {
                if(currentClickID.match("^article_") && !currentClickID.match("^article_abstract_CC")) {   
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "An All-Phosphate and Zero-Strain Sodium-Ion Battery Based on Na&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode, NaTi&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Anode, and Trimethyl Phosphate Electrolyte with Intrinsic Safety and Long Lifespan", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b14946", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                }
            }
        });
        
        // Access Management icons hover
        var articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        var articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent === false) {
                articleAccessManagementIconHover = true;
                var articleAccessManagementHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleAccessManagementIconHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "An All-Phosphate and Zero-Strain Sodium-Ion Battery Based on Na&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode, NaTi&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Anode, and Trimethyl Phosphate Electrolyte with Intrinsic Safety and Long Lifespan", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b14946", "Article_Element": articleAccessManagementHover });
    
                        articleAccessManagementIconHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_access_icon']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAccessManagementIconHover = false;
        });
    
        // articleRightsPermissionsLink hover
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        var articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = false;
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent === false) {
                articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = true;
                var articleRightsHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if(articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover === true) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "An All-Phosphate and Zero-Strain Sodium-Ion Battery Based on Na&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode, NaTi&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Anode, and Trimethyl Phosphate Electrolyte with Intrinsic Safety and Long Lifespan", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b14946", "Article_Element": articleRightsHover });
    
                        articleRightsPermissionsLinkHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_rights_permissions']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleRightsPermissionsLinkHover = false;
        });
    
        // Author hover
        var articleAuthorHover = false
        var articleAuthorHoverEvent = false
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if((articleAuthorHoverEvent === false) && ($(this).parent().hasClass("view-affs") === false)) {
                articleAuthorHover = true;
                var authorInfoHover =  $(this).attr("data-id") + "_hover";
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAuthorHover === true) && (articleAuthorHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "An All-Phosphate and Zero-Strain Sodium-Ion Battery Based on Na&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode, NaTi&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Anode, and Trimethyl Phosphate Electrolyte with Intrinsic Safety and Long Lifespan", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b14946", "Article_Element": authorInfoHover });
    
                        articleAuthorHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $("[data-id='article_author_info']").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            articleAuthorHover = false;
        });
    
        // CC License hover
        var articleAbstractCCHover = false
        var articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = false
        var articleDrawerCCHover = false
        var articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = false
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseenter", function(e) {
            if($(this).attr("data-id")) {
                if(($(this).attr("data-id") === "article_drawer_CC-License") && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleDrawerCCHover = true;
                    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleDrawerCCHover === true) && (articleDrawerCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "An All-Phosphate and Zero-Strain Sodium-Ion Battery Based on Na&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode, NaTi&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Anode, and Trimethyl Phosphate Electrolyte with Intrinsic Safety and Long Lifespan", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b14946", "Article_Element": "article_drawer_CC-License_hover" });
    
                            articleDrawerCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
                else if(($(this).attr("data-id").match("^article_abstract_CC")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                    articleAbstractCCHover = true;
    
                    setTimeout(function() { 
                        if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                            gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "An All-Phosphate and Zero-Strain Sodium-Ion Battery Based on Na&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode, NaTi&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Anode, and Trimethyl Phosphate Electrolyte with Intrinsic Safety and Long Lifespan", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b14946", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                            articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                        }
                    }, 1000);
                }
            }
            else if(($(this).hasClass("article__cc-license__link")) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = true;
                
                setTimeout(function() { 
                    if((articleAbstractCCHover === true) && (articleAbstractCCHoverEvent === false)) {
                        gtag("event", "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "An All-Phosphate and Zero-Strain Sodium-Ion Battery Based on Na&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode, NaTi&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Anode, and Trimethyl Phosphate Electrolyte with Intrinsic Safety and Long Lifespan", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b14946", "Article_Element": "article_abstract_CC_hover" });
    
                        articleAbstractCCHoverEvent = true;
                    }
                }, 1000);
            }
        });
        $(".article__cc-license__inter a").on("mouseleave", function(e) {
            if(articleAbstractCCHover === true) {
                articleAbstractCCHover = false;
            }
            if(articleDrawerCCHover = true) {
                articleDrawerCCHover = false;
            }
        });
        
        // show recommeneded click delay
        var intervalCount = 0;
        var showRecommendedInterval = setInterval(function() {
            intervalCount += 100;
            if($(".show-recommended__wrapper .show-recommended").length > 0) {
                clearInterval(showRecommendedInterval);
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowMore']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "An All-Phosphate and Zero-Strain Sodium-Ion Battery Based on Na&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode, NaTi&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Anode, and Trimethyl Phosphate Electrolyte with Intrinsic Safety and Long Lifespan", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b14946", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
                $("[data-id='article_drawer_RecommendedShowLess']").on("mousedown", function(e) {
                    gtag('event', "Journal Article", { "Article_Title": "An All-Phosphate and Zero-Strain Sodium-Ion Battery Based on Na&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt;V&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Cathode, NaTi&lt;sub&gt;2&lt;/sub&gt;(PO&lt;sub&gt;4&lt;/sub&gt;)&lt;sub&gt;3&lt;/sub&gt; Anode, and Trimethyl Phosphate Electrolyte with Intrinsic Safety and Long Lifespan", "Article_DOI": "10.1021/acsami.7b14946", "Article_Element": $(this).attr("data-id") });
                });
            }
        }, 100);
    }
});

author-aff-symbol"><sup>â </sup></span></span></li><li><span><span class="hlFld-ContribAuthor" data-id="article_author_info" property="author"><a R. China</span></div><div class="corresp-info"><strong>*</strong>E-mail: <a href="mailto:ylcao@whu.edu.cn">ylcao@whu.edu.cn</a></div></div></div><div class="article_header-footer"><div class="article_header-footer-left"><div class="article_header-links"><input class="pub-doi" type="hidden" name="pub-doi" value="10.1021/acsami.7b14946"><a href="/doi/epdf/10.1021/acsami.7b14946?ref=article_openPDF" title="PDF" target="_blank" class="article__btn__secondary" data-id="article_header_OpenPDF"><i class="icon-open-pdf"></i><span>Open PDF</span></a><a href="/servlet/linkout?suffix=s0&amp;dbid=16384&amp;doi=10.1021/acsami.7b14946&amp;type=refOpenUrl&amp;url=http%3A%2F%2Fimp-primo.hosted.exlibrisgroup.com%2Fopenurl%2F44IMP%2FICL_VU1%3Fid%3Ddoi%3A10.1021%252Facsami.7b14946%26sid%3Dliteratum%253Aachs%26pmid%3D29171750%26genre%3Darticle%26aulast%3DJiang%26date%3D2017%26atitle%3DAn%2BAll-Phosphate%2Band%2BZero-Strain%2BSodium-Ion%2BBattery%2BBased%2Bon%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25293%2BCathode%252C%2BNaTi2%2528PO4%25293%2BAnode%252C%2Band%2BTrimethyl%2BPhosphate%2BElectrolyte%2Bwith%2BIntrinsic%2BSafety%2Band%2BLong%2BLifespan%26jtitle%3DACS%2BApplied%2BMaterials%2B%2526%2BInterfaces%26title%3DACS%2BApplied%2BMaterials%2B%2526%2BInterfaces%26volume%3D9%26issue%3D50%26spage%3D43733%26epage%3D43738%26issn%3D1944-8244" title="OpenURL IMPERIAL COLLEGE LONDON" class="issue-item_open-url sfxLink"><img src="/userimages/9157ccea-6c85-4e5f-ac2a-6a9fd9422c17/sfxbutton-180e067c810" alt="OpenURL IMPERIAL COLLEGE LONDON"></a></div></div></div><div class="article_header-meta"><div class="article_header-meta-left"><input type="hidden" name="journalCodeForjhpLink" value="aamick"><input type="hidden" name="journalNameForjhpLink" value="ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces"><div class="article_header-journal"><h2>ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</h2></div><div class="article_header-cite-this" tabindex="0"><input type="hidden" name="citation-copy-value" value="ACS Appl. Empty dropzone --></div></div></div></div><div class="article_abstract"><div class="article_abstract-title" id="Abstract" tabindex="0"><h2>Abstract</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div><div class="article_abstract-content hlFld-Abstract" id="abstractBox" property="description"><figure id="f_tgr1" data-index="0" class="article__inlineFigure article_abstract-img"><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img class="inline-fig internalNav" src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/medium/am-2017-14946j_0007.gif" alt="" id="tgr1" property="image" style="width:405px; height:275px"></button><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/large/am-2017-14946j_0007.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b14946&amp;id=f_tgr1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><p class="articleBody_abstractText">Development of intrinsically safe and long lifespan sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) is urgently needed for large-scale energy storage applications. However, most of the currently developed SIBs suffer from insufficient cycle life and potential unsafety. Herein, we construct an all-phosphate sodium-ion battery (AP-SIB) using a Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode, NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> anode, and nonflammable trimethyl phosphate (TMP) electrolyte. The AP-SIB exhibits not only high safety, high rate performance, and ultralong cycle life but also zero-strain characteristics due to the inverse volume change of the phosphate cathode and anode during charge and discharge cycles, offering a safer and cycle-stable Na-ion technology for electric storage applications.</p></div><div class="article__cc-license"><div class="article__cc-license__body"><p class="article__cc-license__para">This publication is licensed under the terms of your
                            institutional subscription.
                            <a href="/servlet/linkout?type=rightslink&amp;url=startPage%3D43733%26pageCount%3D6%26copyright%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26author%3DXiaoyu%2BJiang%252C%2BZiqi%2BZeng%252C%2BLifen%2BXiao%252C%2Bet%2Bal%26orderBeanReset%3Dtrue%26imprint%3DAmerican%2BChemical%2BSociety%26volumeNum%3D9%26issueNum%3D50%26contentID%3Dacsami.7b14946%26title%3DAn%2BAll-Phosphate%2Band%2BZero-Strain%2BSodium-Ion%2BBattery%2BBased%2Bon%2BNa3V2%2528PO4%25293%2BCathode%252C%2BNaTi2%2528PO4%25293%2BAnode%252C%2Band%2BTrimethyl%2BPhosphate%2BElectrolyte%2Bwith%2BIntrinsic%2BSafety%2Band%2BLong%2BLifespan%26numPages%3D6%26pa%3D%26issn%3D1944-8244%26publisherName%3Dacs%26publication%3Daamick%26rpt%3Dn%26endPage%3D43738%26publicationDate%3DDecember%2B2017" class="link--bold">Request reuse permissions.</a></p></div></div><span class="hidden" property="publisher">ACS Publications</span><div class="article_header-article-copyright">Copyright Â© 2017 American Chemical Society</div><div class="article_header-footer-right"><div class="articleHeaderDropzone7" data-pb-dropzone="articleHeaderDropzone7"><div class="article__tags article__tags--subjects"><div class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Subjects</h3><div tabindex="0" class="article__tags__tooltip"><div aria-describedby="tooltip-subjects" class="article__tags__icon"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are subjects</span></div><p id="tooltip-subjects" role="tooltip" class="article__tags__diff">Article subjects are automatically applied from the ACS Subject Taxonomy and describe the scientific concepts and themes of the article.</p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291517&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Batteries" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Batteries" class="article__tags__link">Batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=291371&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrodes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrodes" class="article__tags__link">Electrodes</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=292120&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Electrolytes" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Electrolytes" class="article__tags__link">Electrolytes</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"><a href="/action/doSearch?ConceptID=290673&amp;ref=fulltext" title="Inorganic carbon compounds" data-id="article_abstract_Subject_Inorganic%20carbon%20compounds" class="article__tags__container"><header class="article__tags__header"><h3 class="article__tags__heading">Keywords</h3><div class="article__tags__tooltip" tabindex="0"><div class="article__tags__icon" aria-describedby="tooltip-keywords"><i class="icon-info-circle-outline"></i><span class="sr-only">what are keywords</span></div><p class="article__tags__diff" id="tooltip-keywords" role="tooltip">
                        Article keywords are supplied by the authors and highlight key terms and topics
                        of the paper.
                    </p></div></header><ul class="article__tags__list"><li class="article__tags__item"><a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Phosphate&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_phosphate">phosphate</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Safety&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_safety">safety</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Zero-strain&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_zero-strain">zero-strain</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Sodium-ion+Batteries&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_sodium-ion%20batteries">sodium-ion batteries</a></li><li class="article__tags__item"> <a class="article__tags__link" href="https://pubs.acs.org/action/doSearch?action=search&amp;AllField=Energy+Storage&amp;qsSearchArea=AllField&amp;ref=fulltext" data-id="article_abstract_Keyword_energy%20storage">energy storage</a></li></ul></div></div></div><div class="article_content"><div class="article_content-table hlFld-FullText"><div class="article_content-row"><div class="article_content-left" property="articleBody"><div id="sec1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i1">1 Introduction</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">Electrical energy storage (EES) technologies with low cost, environmental friendliness, and high safety are now extensively pursued for effective utilization of renewable energy sources. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref1 ref2 ref3 ref4 ref5" aria-label="reference 1 to 5">(1-5)</a> Compared with the various currently developed EES technologies, sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have competitive advantages because of the adequate supply and low cost of Na resources and similar battery chemistry to lithium-ion batteries. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6 ref7 ref8 ref9'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref6 ref7 ref8 ref9" aria-label="reference 6 to 9">(6-9)</a> Currently, most SIBs use highly flammable and volatile organic carbonate esters as electrolytes, which can cause potential safety problems of SIBs, especially for large-scale energy storage applications. When the batteries are subjected to abuse such as short-circuiting, crush, overcharge, overheating or high temperature impact, a series of side reactions among the anode, cathode, and electrolyte would cause a catastrophic thermal runaway, even resulting in firing or explosion. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref10 ref11'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref10 ref11" aria-label="reference 10 and 11">(10, 11)</a> There is an urgent need to develop radically new electrolytes with high safety.</div><div class="NLM_p">Aqueous electrolytes and solid-state electrolytes are considered to be alternative electrolytes for constructing safer SIBs. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref12 ref13 ref14 ref15 ref16'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref12 ref13 ref14 ref15 ref16" aria-label="reference 12 to 16">(12-16)</a> However, aqueous SIBs suffer from low operation voltage and dissolution of most electrode-active materials, leading to low energy density and insufficient cyclability. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref17 ref18 ref19'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref17 ref18 ref19" aria-label="reference 17 to 19">(17-19)</a> Despite that a number of solid-state electrolytes are reported for SIBs, their low room temperature conductivities and poor interfacial compatibility may only allow low rate applications. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref20'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref20" aria-label="reference 20">(20)</a> Therefore, it is still a must to develop a safe electrolyte with a wide electrochemical window and high ionic conductivity for practical battery applications. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref21 ref22 ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref21 ref22 ref23" aria-label="reference 21 to 23">(21-23)</a> In the search for such a safer electrolyte, organic phosphates appear to be a promising candidate due to their nonflammability, high solvating ability, and low viscosity for electrolyte salts. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23 ref24 ref25'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23 ref24 ref25" aria-label="reference 23 to 25">(23-25)</a> As a proof of concept, we have reported a proton-type SIB based on dimethyl methyl phosphonate (DMMP), demonstrating the safer SIB can be achieved using this class of electrolytes. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref23'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref23" aria-label="reference 23">(23)</a></div><div class="NLM_p">Except for the safer electrolyte, electrode materials with high thermal stability and long lifespan are also key issues for battery applications. In the past decade, lots of host materials, such as metal oxide, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref26 ref27 ref28 ref29 ref30 ref31 ref32 ref33'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref26 ref27 ref28 ref29 ref30 ref31 ref32 ref33" aria-label="reference 26 to 33">(26-33)</a> phosphate <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref34 ref35'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref34 ref35" aria-label="reference 34 and 35">(34, 35)</a> and ferrocyanide cathodes, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref36 ref37 ref38'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref36 ref37 ref38" aria-label="reference 36 to 38">(36-38)</a> metal alloys, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref39 ref40 ref41'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref39 ref40 ref41" aria-label="reference 39 to 41">(39-41)</a> and carbonaceous anodes, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref42 ref43 ref44'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref42 ref43 ref44" aria-label="reference 42 to 44">(42-44)</a> have been investigated for Na-storage electrodes. However, few of them have exhibited sufficient long-term cycle stability and thermal stability. NASICON phosphate hosts such as cathodic Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and anodic NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> have large-sized 3D tunnels and a stable lattice structure, which can enable fast Na<sup>+</sup> ion transport and zero-strain insertion reaction during cycling, leading to high rate capacity and long lifespan. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref35 ref45 ref46 ref47'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref35 ref45 ref46 ref47" aria-label="reference 35 and 45 to 47">(35, 45-47)</a> Therefore, these thermostable phosphate frameworks could be coupled with nonflammable electrolytes to build safer and cycle-stable SIBs.</div><div class="NLM_p last">In this paper, we propose an all-phosphate sodium-ion battery (AP-SIB) using a Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVP) cathode and NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NTP) anode, coupled with nonflammable phosphate electrolyte (trimethyl phosphate, TMP). Both the Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode and NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> anode showed excellent adaptability to the TMP-based electrolyte, rendering cycling stability and rate capability comparable to that in a conventional carbonate electrolyte. In addition, the AP-SIB full cells show high safety even in fire due to their intrinsic nonflammability. Moreover, the AP-SIBs exhibit zero-strain characteristics due to the inverse volume changes of the phosphate cathode and anode during charge and discharge, <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref48 ref49'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref48 ref49" aria-label="reference 48 and 49">(48, 49)</a> leading to excellent cycling performance (56 mAh g<sup>â1</sup> after 1000 cycles at 10 C, 73.7% capacity retention) and designing flexibility for practical application.</div></div><div id="sec2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i2">2 Experimental Methods</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div id="sec2-1" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i3" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i3">2.1 Materials</h3><div class="NLM_p last">Trimethyl phosphate (TMP) and fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) were purchased from Aladdin and purified by distillation under vacuum before use. Graphene oxide (GO) suspension was obtained from Shandong Yuhuang New Energy Technology Co., Ltd.</div></div><div id="sec2-2" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i4" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i4">2.2 Preparation of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/rGO (NVP/rGO) Composite</h3><div class="NLM_p last">V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub>, NH<sub>4</sub>H<sub>2</sub>PO<sub>4</sub>, and Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> first were dispersed in water with a stoichiometric ratio. Oxalic acid (V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub>:Oxalic acid = 1:4, molar ratio) was added into the solution during stirring at 70 Â°C. When the solution became transparent, an appropriate amount of GO dispersion was added (5 mg mL<sup>â1</sup>) with vigorous stirring. The NVP/GO precursor was prepared by a spray-drying process at the outlet temperature of 290 Â°C and then heated in flowing Ar at 850 Â°C for 8 h with a heating rate of 2 Â°C min<sup>â1</sup> to form the NVP/rGO.</div></div><div id="sec2-3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i5" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i5">2.3 Preparation of NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>/rGO (NTP/rGO) Composite</h3><div class="NLM_p last">P25 powder (20 mmol) was dispersed in 80 mL of aqueous solution containing Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> (5 mmol) and NH<sub>4</sub>H<sub>2</sub>PO<sub>4</sub> (30 mmol). Then, 81 mL of GO suspension (5 mg mL<sup>â1</sup>) was added into the solution with vigorous stirring. The NTP/GO precursor was prepared by a spray-drying process at the outlet temperature of 290 Â°C and then heated in flowing Ar at 850 Â°C for 8 h with a heating rate of 2 Â°C min<sup>â1</sup> to form the NTP/rGO.</div></div><div id="sec2-4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i6" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i6">2.4 Materials Characterization</h3><div class="NLM_p last">X-ray diffraction (XRD) was performed on a Shimazdu, model LabX XRD-6000 instrument. Field-emission scanning electron microscopy (FESEM) was performed by a field-emission scanning electron microscope operated at 5 kV (Merlin VP Compact, Carl Zeiss, Germany). Transmission electron microscopy (TEM) was performed using a field-emission transmission electron microscope (JEM-2100 HR). The ionic conductivity of the electrolytes was measured by using a conductivity measuring meter (DDS-307, Leici, China) at 20â40 Â°C. Thermal analysis of the electrodes was carried out on a differential scanning calorimetry (DSC, Q200 TA) at a heating rate of 10 Â°C min<sup>â1</sup> from 60 to 450 Â°C.</div></div><div id="sec2-5" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_2"><div id="ac_i7" class="anchor-spacer"></div><h3 class="article-section__title" id="_i7">2.5 Electrochemical Measurement</h3><div class="NLM_p last">The electrode films were prepared by mixing NVP/rGO or NTP/rGO with acetylene black and poly(vinyl difluoride) (PVdF) in <i>N</i>-methyl-2-pyrrolidinone (7:2:1, weight ratio). The obtained slurry was pasted on a Cu foil, followed by drying in vacuum at 100 Â°C for 12 h. The 2016-type coin half-cells with sodium foil as the counter electrode and 0.8 M NaClO<sub>4</sub> in trimethyl phosphate (TMP) as the electrolyte were assembled in an argon-filled glovebox with both O<sub>2</sub> and H<sub>2</sub>O &lt; 1 ppm. In the half-cell, to improve the reversibility of the Na electrode, the electrolyte contains 10 vol % fluoroethylene carbonate as film-forming additive. The all-phosphate-based sodium-ion battery was constructed by the NTP/rGO anode and NVP/rGO cathode with a mass ratio of 1:1.1 in the 0.8 M NaClO<sub>4</sub>/TMP electrolyte. The cells were cycled on a LAND battery tester (Wuhan LAND Electronics Co., China) between 2.0 and 3.9 V for the NVP/rGO half-cell, 1.4â3.0 V for the NTP/rGO half-cell, and 0.4â2.0 V for the all-phosphate full cell, respectively. Cyclic voltammetry (CV) tests were performed using an electrochemical workstation (Autolab PGSTAT128N, Eco Chemie, Netherlands).</div></div></div><div id="sec3" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i8">3 Results and Discussion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p">The Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVP) and NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NTP) particles coated with reduced graphene oxide (rGO) in this work were synthesized by a facile spray-drying method as described in our previous work. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref50 ref51'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref50 ref51" aria-label="reference 50 and 51">(50, 51)</a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig1" aria-label="Figure 1">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>a,d shows the XRD patterns of the NVP/rGO and NTP/rGO samples, respectively. All the diffraction peaks of these two compounds are indexed to the <i>R</i>3Ì<i>c</i> space group, NASICON structure (JCPDF card No. 53-0018 for NVP and No. 85-2265 for NTP), indicating high crystallinity and purity. The typical FESEM images (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig1" aria-label="Figure 1">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>b,e) show that both the NVP/rGO and NTP/rGO particles appear as a spherical morphology with a diameter of about 10 Î¼m. The TEM images (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig1" aria-label="Figure 1">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>c,f) show that both the NVP/rGO and NTP/rGO microspheres consist of smaller irregular-structured nanoparticles. The high-resolution TEM images of the microspheres in the insets of <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig1" aria-label="Figure 1">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig1" id="" class=" internalNav">1</a>c,f reveal that the NVP and TMP surfaces are tightly coated by uniform graphene-coating layers through spray-drying and calcination, which would form fast electron transport channels for electrochemical reaction.</div><figure id="fig1" data-index="1" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 1</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/medium/am-2017-14946j_0001.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/large/am-2017-14946j_0001.jpeg" id="gr1" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 1. (a, d) XRD patterns, (b, e) SEM images, and (c, f) TEM images of the NVP/rGO and NTP/rGO powders, respectively. The insets show the enlarge TEM image of NVP/rGO (c) and high-resolution TEM image of NTP/rGO (f).</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/large/am-2017-14946j_0001.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b14946&amp;id=fig1"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The ionic conductivity of the TMP electrolyte at the temperature range of â20 to 40 Â°C is shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>a. The 0.8 M NaClO<sub>4</sub>/TMP electrolyte possesses an ionic conductivity of 5.41 mS cm<sup>â1</sup> at 25 Â°C, which is slightly lower than that (â¼6.3 mS cm<sup>â1</sup>) of carbonate electrolyte. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref52'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref52" aria-label="reference 52">(52)</a> The flammability tests (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>b) reveal that the TMP electrolyte cannot be ignited, demonstrating strong fire retardancy. <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>c shows the CV curves of the Pt microelectrode in TMP-based electrolyte. No apparent redox peak could be observed at 0â5.0 V vs Na<sup>+</sup>/Na except for the plating/stripping peaks of sodium metal, indicating a wide electrochemical window for the TMP electrolyte up to 5 V. <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig2" aria-label="Figure 2">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig2" id="" class=" internalNav">2</a>d displays the CV curves of TMP-based electrolyte on NVP/rGO and NTP/rGO electrodes. The NVP/rGO electrode and NTP/rGO electrode show a pair of peaks around 3.4 and 2.1 V, corresponding to the reversible transformation of V<sup>3+</sup>/V<sup>4+</sup> and Ti<sup>3+</sup>/Ti<sup>4+</sup>, respectively.</div><figure id="fig2" data-index="2" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 2</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/medium/am-2017-14946j_0002.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/large/am-2017-14946j_0002.jpeg" id="gr2" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 2. (a) Arrhenius plot, (b) flame tests of the 0.8 M NaClO<sub>4</sub>/TMP + 10 vol % FEC electrolyte. Cyclic voltammograms of the 0.8 M NaClO<sub>4</sub>/TMP + 10 vol % FEC electrolyte on the (c) Pt microelectrode (10 mV s<sup>â1</sup>) and (d) NVP/rGO and NTP/rGO electrode (0.1 mV s<sup>â1</sup>).</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/large/am-2017-14946j_0002.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b14946&amp;id=fig2"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The electrochemical performances of the NVP/rGO cathode and NTP/rGO anode evaluated in the TMP electrolyte are shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>. The discharge capacities of the NVP/rGO electrode are 116.0, 115.9, 111.3, 106.9, 95.7, 81.3, 58.6, and 40.6 mAh g<sup>â1</sup> at the rate of 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5, 10, 20, and 30 C, respectively (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>a). <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>c shows the cycling performance of the NVP/rGO cathode in the TMP electrolyte at 0.5 C. Very impressively, the NVP/rGO exhibits a discharge capacity of 102.9 mA h g<sup>â1</sup> after 1000 cycles, corresponding to 89.8% capacity retention. <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>b displays the rate performance of the NTP/rGO anode at various current densities. The charge capacities at 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5, 10, 20, and 30 C are 127.8, 122.7, 117.7, 111.7, 104, 96.2, 87, and 80.6 mAh g<sup>â1</sup>, respectively. It is noted that a small sluggish peak appeared at starting the charging process at 0.2 C. This phenomenon may result from the polarization during the initial few cycles. After full activation of the electrode, the small sluggish peak disappeared. Besides, two discharge plateaus could be observed at relatively high current densities (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>b). This is commonly ascribed to the transfer of Na<sup>+</sup> from the Na(1) to the Na(2) sites as local temperature increase induced by high current rates. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref45'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref45" aria-label="reference 45">(45)</a> A similar phenomenon has also been reported for other NASICON-type materials. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref53 ref54'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref53 ref54" aria-label="reference 53 and 54">(53, 54)</a><a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig3" aria-label="Figure 3">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig3" id="" class=" internalNav">3</a>d shows the cycling stability of the NTP/rGO electrode at 0.5 C in the TMP electrolyte. The NTP/rGO electrode delivers a charge capacity of 91.4 mA h g<sup>â1</sup> after 1000 cycles, corresponding to 74% capacity retention, which is similar to that (77%) in the carbonate electrolyte. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref51'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref51" aria-label="reference 51">(51)</a> The high cycling Coulombic efficiencies (&gt;99.5%) of both NVP/rGO and NTP/rGO electrodes indicate high electrochemical compatibility with the TMP electrolyte, ensuring long-term cycling stability. This superior cycle stability is difficult to obtain in aqueous electrolyte, due to some unavoidable side reactions such as hydrogen and oxygen evolutions especially at low current rates or at overcharge.</div><figure id="fig3" data-index="3" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 3</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/medium/am-2017-14946j_0003.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/large/am-2017-14946j_0003.jpeg" id="gr3" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 3. (a, b) Rate performances and (c, d) cycling performances at 0.5 C rate of the NVP/rGO and NTP/rGO electrodes in the TMP electrolyte, respectively.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/large/am-2017-14946j_0003.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b14946&amp;id=fig3"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The thermal stabilities of the NVP and NTP electrodes in the phosphate and carbonate electrolytes were comparatively investigated by differential scanning calorimetry (DSC) in the full charging state and discharging state, respectively (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig4" aria-label="Figure 4">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig4" id="" class=" internalNav">4</a>). The NVP and NTP electrodes show the exothermic peaks at 333.9 and 417.4 Â°C with a heat generation of 234.0 and 94.8 J g<sup>â1</sup> in the TMP electrolyte, respectively. In contrast, the NVP and NTP exhibit lower exothermic peaks at 323.3 and 295.4 Â°C and increased heat generation of 240.8 and 106.2 J g<sup>â1</sup> in the carbonate electrolyte, respectively. Therefore, it is evident that the TMP electrolyte can greatly improve thermal stability and safety of sodium-ion batteries compared to the carbonate electrolyte. <a onclick="showRef(event, 'ref55'); return false;" href="javascript:void(0);" class="ref ref55" aria-label="reference 55">(55)</a></div><figure id="fig4" data-index="4" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 4</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/medium/am-2017-14946j_0004.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/large/am-2017-14946j_0004.jpeg" id="gr4" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 4. Comparison of the DSC profiles of (a) charged NVP and (b) discharged NTP in TMP and carbonated electrolytes.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/large/am-2017-14946j_0004.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b14946&amp;id=fig4"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">Encouraged by the electrochemical compatibility of the phosphate electrodes in phosphate electrolyte, we construct an intrinsically safe all-phosphate sodium-ion battery (AP-SIB) using the NVP/rGO cathode and NTP/rGO anode along with the TMP electrolyte. The NVP/rGO and NTP/rGO materials were balanced with the mass ratio of 1.1:1 based on their initial capacities. The full cell exhibits a potential plateau around 1.25 V in the first cycle with a discharge capacity of 103.7 mAh g<sup>â1</sup> and Coulombic efficiency of 87.7% at 0.2 C (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig5" aria-label="Figure 5">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>a). At a current rate of 0.2, 0.5, 1, 2, 5, 10, and 20 C, the cell delivers a discharge capacity of 103.7, 99.7, 88.7, 82.2, 74.6, 61.4, and 37.8 mAh g<sup>â1</sup>, respectively. The capacity can be recovered to 94.7 mAh g<sup>â1</sup> as the current is returned to 0.5 C (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig5" aria-label="Figure 5">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>b), suggesting excellent reversibility and rate capability. Considering the total mass weight of the NVP and NTP, a Ragone plot (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig5" aria-label="Figure 5">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>d) was drawn to show the dependence of the energy density on the power density of the cell, based on the galvanostatic charge/discharge curves shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig5" aria-label="Figure 5">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>c. The results in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig5" aria-label="Figure 5">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>d clearly demonstrate that the specific energy of the NTP//NVP cell in TMP electrolyte is 68.1 and 16.01 Wh kg<sup>â1</sup> at a power density of 13.4 and 847.3 W kg<sup>â1</sup>, respectively, indicating high energy output even at high power density. <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig5" aria-label="Figure 5">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig5" id="" class=" internalNav">5</a>e presents the long-term cycling performance of the AP-SIB cell (0.2 C for the first four cycles and 10 C for the subsequent cycles). The AP-SIB cell exhibits a discharge capacity of around 56 mAh g<sup>â1</sup> after 1000 cycles (73.7% capacity retention) with the Coulombic efficiency of 99.7%, exhibiting highly reversible Na storage performance. The high Coulombic efficiency (&gt;99.5%) of the AP-SIB during cycling is most likely due to the absence of any detrimental side reaction (or SEI formation) of the TMP electrolyte in the operating voltage region.</div><figure id="fig5" data-index="5" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 5</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/medium/am-2017-14946j_0005.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/large/am-2017-14946j_0005.jpeg" id="gr5" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 5. (a) Typical charge/discharge curve at 0.2 C, (b) rate performance, (c) typical chargeâdischarge profiles at various current rates, (d) Ragone plot of rate capability, and (e) cycling performance for the all-phosphate-based full cell.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/large/am-2017-14946j_0005.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b14946&amp;id=fig5"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure><div class="NLM_p">The XRD patterns of the NVP/rGO and NTP/rGO electrodes before and after cycling are shown in <a class="ref internalNav" href="#fig6" aria-label="Figure 6">Figure </a><a data-tab="pane-pcw-Figures" href="#fig6" id="" class=" internalNav">6</a>. After refining the XRD data (<a class="ref internalNav" href="#tbl1" aria-label="Table 1">Table </a><a class="ref showTableEvent internalNav" data-id="tbl1" href="#tbl1">1</a>), the volume change of the NVP/rGO cathode declined 7.88% in the charge state while the NTP/rGO anode increased by 7.55% in the discharge state. This indicates that the AP-SIB would remain almost zero volume change during charging and discharging, which facilitates to realize long-term cyclability and flexible structure design for the large-capacity battery.</div><div class="NLM_table-wrap" id="tbl1"><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption"><div class="NLM_caption" id=""><div class="title2">Table 1. Main Refinement Parameters of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and Volume Variations of AP-AIB Full Cell after Charging</div></div></div><div class="scrollable-table-wrap"><table class="table" border="0"><colgroup><col align="left"><col align="left"><col align="char" char="."><col data-index="6" class="article__inlineFigure"><h2 class="fig-label">Figure 6</h2><button class="figure-viewer__trigger" aria-label="open figure viewer"><img src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/medium/am-2017-14946j_0006.gif" alt="" data-lg-src="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/large/am-2017-14946j_0006.jpeg" id="gr6" class="inline-fig internalNav"></button><figcaption><div class="hlFld-FigureCaption caption"><p class="first last">Figure 6. Rietveld refined fits of the XRD patterns for (a) Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, (b) NaV<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, (c) NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>, and (d) Na<sub>3</sub>Ti<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>.</p></div></figcaption><div class="figure-bottom-links"><div class="download-hi-res-img"><a title="High Resolution Image" href="/cms/10.1021/acsami.7b14946/asset/images/large/am-2017-14946j_0006.jpeg"><span>High Resolution Image</span></a></div><div class="download-ppt"><a title="Download MS PowerPoint Slide" href="/action/downloadFigures?doi=10.1021/acsami.7b14946&amp;id=fig6"><span>Download MS PowerPoint Slide</span></a></div></div></figure></div><div id="sec4" class="NLM_sec NLM_sec_level_1"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="_i10">4 Conclusion</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><div class="NLM_p last">In summary, an intrinsically safe and zero-strain all-phosphate sodium-ion battery (AP-SIB) with high rate capacity and long lifespan has been successfully developed for the first time by adopting NASCION NTP and NVP electrodes and nonflammable TMP electrolyte. The NTP anode and NVP cathode not only have a highly stable structure but also have high thermal safety. The TMP electrolyte offers appropriate ionic conductivity and high electrochemical stability in the operating potential range for regular battery function, and intrinsically fire resistance to ensure high thermal stability. As a result, the AP-SIB exhibits considerable discharge capacity (102.9 mAh g<sup>â1</sup>) at 0.2 C based on the NVP/rGO cathode, long cyclic life up to 1000 cycles with 73.7% capacity retention at 10 C, and high rate capacity (61.4 mAh g<sup>â1</sup> at 10 C and 37.8 mAh g<sup>â1</sup> at 20 C). Furthermore, the AP-SIB efficiently avoids firing as usually encountered in the carbonate electrolyte and severe side reactions such as hydrogen and oxygen evolution in the aqueous electrolyte, demonstrating high safety, long lifespan, and high energy/power densities for energy storage applications. Particularly, the AP-SIB possesses zero-strain characteristics which not only guarantees long cycling performance but also provides elastic structure design for large-capacity systems, rendering a new avenue toward highly safe and stable sodium-ion batteries.</div></div><div class="NLM_back"><div class="article_supporting-info" id="_suppInfo"></div><div class="testing" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.7b14946" data-url="https://widgets.figshare.com/static/figshare.js" id="figshare-widget"></div><div class="authorInformationSection"><div class="article_content-header"><div class="article_content-header-row"><div class="article_content-title" tabindex="0"><h2 id="authorInformationSection">Author Information</h2><div class="article__copy"><button class="article__copy__btn"><i class="article__copy__icon icon-copy-solid" aria-hidden="true"></i></button><span class="article__copy__text">Click to copy section link</span><span class="article__copy__success">Section link copied!</span></div></div></div></div><hr><ul><li><span class="author-information-subsection-header">Corresponding Author</span><ul><li><div class="authorItemInformation"><span class="hlFld-ContribAuthor strong">Yuliang Cao</span> - <span class="hlFld-Affiliation affiliation">College of Chemistry

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Sodium manganese hexacyanoferrate cathode materials with two structures can be synthesized at room temp.  The sodium-ion concn. in the aq. soln. during pptn. has a strong influence on the compn. and structure of the final product, resulting in different reversible capacity and cycling performance.  With higher Na+ concn., a cooperative Na+ displacement along a single [111] direction induces a transition from cubic to rhombohedral symmetry - this phase transition is reversible on cycling the Na+ concn.  Sodium manganese hexacyanoferrate with an initial rhombohedral structure exhibits a reversible capacity of 134 mA-h/g and retains 120 mA-h/g after 30 cycles.  The high power d. and high rate capability of this material make it a promising cathode material for rechargeable SIBs.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGqkcibGQmYRi7Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lhPRfDPoS1cIw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC3sXosFOltg%253D%253D&amp;md5=bf39a72c1fe501ee77d73e5353bda8a2</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref2'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit2" data-doi="10.1002/adma.201502018"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Fang, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ai, X.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Cao, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yang, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Hierarchical Carbon Framework Wrapped Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> as a Superior High-Rate and Extended Lifespan Cathode for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Adv.                         cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Flexible Aqueous Lithium-Ion Battery with High Safety and Large Volumetric Energy Density</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Dong, Xiaoli; Chen, Long; Su, Xiuli; Wang, Yonggang; Xia, Yongyao</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2016</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">55</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A flexible and wearable aq. lithium-ion battery is introduced based on spinel Li1.1Mn2O4 cathode and a carbon-coated NASICON-type LiTi2(PO4)3 anode (NASICON=sodium-ion super ionic conductor).  Energy densities of 63 Wh/kg or 124 mWh/cm3 and power densities of 3 275 W/kg or 11.1 W/cm3 can be obtained, which are seven times larger than the largest reported till now.  The full cell can keep its capacity without significant loss under different bending states, which shows excellent flexibility.  Furthermore, two such flexible cells in series with an operation voltage of 4 V can be compatible with current nonaq. Li-ion batteries.  Therefore, such a flexible cell can potentially be put into practical applications for wearable electronics.  In addn., a self-chargeable unit is realized by integrating a single flexible aq. Li-ion battery with a com. flexible solar cell, which may facilitate the long-time outdoor operation of flexible and wearable electronic devices.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGpg7OwwclsnxbVg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg3bZwGkEQxjw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC28XnsFWltL8%253D&amp;md5=79cb9fe6401804ee4c4e24fa3445769d</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref6'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit6" data-doi="10.1002/ange.201404549"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Yu, H.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Ren, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Xiao, D.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Guo, S.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhu, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Qian, Y.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Gu, L.</span><span class="NLM_x">; </span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Zhou, H.</span><span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">An Ultrastable Anode for Long-Life Room-Temperature Sodium-Ion Batteries</span> <span class="citation_source-journal">Angew.                         cas_cit10R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">10</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An electrochemical-thermal coupled overcharge-to-thermal-runaway model for lithium ion battery</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Ren, Dongsheng; Feng, Xuning; Lu, Languang; Ouyang, Minggao; Zheng, Siqi; Li, Jianqiu; He, Xiangming</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">364</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">328-340</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JPSODZ</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0378-7753</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier B.V.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">This paper presents an electrochem.-thermal coupled overcharge-to-thermal-runaway (TR) model to predict the highly interactive electrochem. and thermal behaviors of lithium ion battery under the overcharge conditions.  In this model, the battery voltage equals the difference between the cathode potential and the anode potential, whereas the temp. is predicted by modeling the combined heat generations, including joule heat, thermal runaway reactions and internal short circuit.  The model can fit well with the adiabatic overcharge tests results at 0.33C, 0.5C and 1C, indicating a good capture of the overcharge-to-TR mechanism.  The modeling anal. based on the validated model helps to quantify the heat generation rates of each heat sources during the overcharge-to-TR process.  And the two thermal runaway reactions including the electrolyte oxidn. reaction and the reaction between deposited lithium and electrolyte are found to contribute most to the heat generations during the overcharge process.  Further modeling anal. on the crit. parameters is performed to find possible solns. for the overcharge problem of lithium ion battery.  Increasing the oxidn. potential of the electrolyte, and increasing the onset temp. of thermal runaway are the two effective ways to improve the overcharge performance of lithium ion battery.</div></div><div class="moreSciFi"><a title="Retrieve detailed record, substances, reactions and more for this article from SciFinder Â®" href="https://scifinder.cas.org/scifinder/view/link_v1/reference.jsf?l=BmxxGlm8wGppX4M7sC8_87Vg90H21EOLACvtfcHk0lg3bZwGkEQxjw"> &gt;&gt; More from SciFinder <sup>Â®</sup></a></div><span class="casRefUrl">https://chemport.cas.org/services/resolver?origin=ACS&amp;resolution=options&amp;coi=1%3ACAS%3A528%3ADC%252BC2sXhtlOrtL3I&amp;md5=7832d2aa8cace2de00aaa8f7e32ebe3b</span></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref11"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" onclick="showRef(event, 'ref11'); return false;" data-citation="" class="refNumLink">11</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit11" data-doi="10.1073/pnas.1314615111"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group">Wong, D.                         cas_cit11R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">11</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nonflammable perfluoropolyether-based electrolytes for lithium batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wong, Dominica H. C.; Thelen, Jacob L.; Fu, Yanbao; Devaux, Didier; Pandya, Ashish A.; Battaglia, Vincent S.; Balsara, Nitash P.; De Simone, Joseph M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Proceedings of the National Academy of Sciences of the United States of America</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">111</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">9</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">3327-3331</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">PNASA6</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">National Academy of Sciences</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The flammability of conventional alkyl carbonate electrolytes hinders the integration of large-scale Li-ion batteries in transportation and grid storage applications. Room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries have attracted great attention particularly in large-scale elec. energy storage applications for renewable energy and smart grid because of the huge abundant sodium resources and low cost.  In this article, a variety of electrode materials including cathodes and anodes as well as electrolytes for room-temp. stationary sodium-ion batteries are briefly reviewed.  We compare the difference in storage behavior between Na and Li in their analogous electrodes and summarize the sodium storage mechanisms in the available electrode materials.  This review also includes some new results from our group and our thoughts on developing new materials.  Some perspectives and directions on designing better materials for practical applications are pointed out based on knowledge from the literature and our experience.  Through this extensive literature review, the search for suitable electrode and electrolyte materials for stationary sodium-ion batteries is still challenging.                         cas_cit22R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">22</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">An electrochemically compatible and flame-retardant electrolyte additive for safe lithium ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wu, Bingbin; Pei, Feng; Wu, Yue; Mao, Rongjun; Ai, Xinping; Yang, Hanxi; Cao, Yuliang</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Power Sources</span>

                        cas_cit23R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">23</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A Safer Sodium-Ion Battery Based on Nonflammable Organic Phosphate Electrolyte</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Zeng Ziqi; Jiang Xiaoyu; Yuan Dingding; Ai Xinping; Yang Hanxi; Cao Yuliang; Li Ran</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced science (Weinheim, Baden-Wurttemberg, Germany)</span>
